Rain lashed parts of the national capital. Visuals from the Parliament showed heavy rain showers in the city.\n\nEarlier today, the Indian Meteorological Department issued a warning of light to moderate rainfall accompanied by light thunderstorms and lightning in isolated areas of Delhi-NCR, Yamunanagar and Kurukshetra.\n\nAreas of Delhi-NCR were expected to receive rainfall today include Seemapuri, Hindon AF station, Ghaziabad, Indirapuram, Chhapraula, Noida, Dadro, Greater Noida, Gurugram and Manesar.\n\nAdditionally, the prediction by IMD also said that rain was expected in areas of Haryana including Karnal, Panipat, Hissar, Hansi, Siwani, Sohana, Rewari, Bawal and Nuh.\n\nOn July 18, rain lashed parts of Delhi, bringing respite from the humid weather.\n\nIn June, the city received the highest rainfall recorded in 88 years. According to the IMD, Delhi experienced 228 mm of rainfall from 8: 30 a.m. on June 27 to 8:30 a.m. on June 28.\n\nA total of 235.5 mm of rain was recorded, marking the maximum rainfall in 24 hours in June since 1936.\n\nHowever, due to rain, water levels in the Yamuna River have risen, prompting the authorities to issue an alert to the residents of Noida villages, situated along the riverbanks. These villagers experienced severe flooding last year during the monsoon season, causing significant inconvenience to residents of both Delhi and Noida.\n\nPreviously, on July 21, the IMD issued an orange alert for several districts of Himachal Pradesh, predicting heavy to very heavy rainfall for the coming week. The weather department also informed that light to moderate rainfall, accompanied by thunderstorms and lightning, is likely to occur in various districts of Himachal Pradesh.\n\nEarlier this month, 70 roads and 51 water supply schemes were hampered due to the heavy rainfall in Himachal Pradesh. Additionally, 84 electricity supply schemes were disrupted due to the weather conditions in the region. The IMD issued a yellow alert, forecasting more showers and a drop in temperatures. Several areas recorded significant rainfall, but the city remains below its July average. Rising Yamuna River levels prompted alerts for Noida villagers. The IMD also predicts rainfall in other parts of India, while the AQI in Delhi remains satisfactory.Early on Wednesday, Delhi-NCR experienced a heavy spell of rain, bringing much-needed relief from the persistent humid weather. The India Meteorological Department (IMD) issued a yellow alert for the national capital and surrounding areas, indicating the possibility of more showers throughout the day. A yellow alert signifies heavy rainfall between 6 cm and 11 cm.\n\nRainfall Statistics\n\nThe rain recorded varied across different parts of the city. Palam received 6.6mm, Pusa 6mm, Mayur Vihar 8.5mm, Ayanagar 0.7mm, and Pitampura 2mm of rainfall. However, Safdarjung, the base station, recorded no rain. Other areas like Lodhi Road and Ridge experienced trace amounts of rain, too minimal to measure.\n\nTemperature and Humidity\n\nWith the onset of rainfall, the maximum and minimum temperatures are expected to hover around 36 and 27 degrees Celsius, respectively. Humidity levels ranged from 65% to 95%. Despite the rainfall, the city's total precipitation for July remains 22% below the normal, with only 118.2mm recorded so far against the average of 151mm.\n\nRising Water Levels in Yamuna\n\nDue to the recent rains, the water levels in the Yamuna River have risen. Authorities have issued alerts to residents of Noida villages situated along the riverbanks. These residents faced severe flooding last year during the monsoon season, causing significant disruption in both Delhi and Noida.\n\nBroader Weather Forecast\n\nThe IMD also predicts heavy rainfall over parts of Gujarat, Madhya Pradesh, and Maharashtra on July 24. The northwestern state of Rajasthan is likely to experience hot, humid weather until tomorrow. Northeastern India is expected to have \"fairly widespread light to moderate rainfall\" over the next five days. Himachal Pradesh has a 'yellow' warning of heavy rains at isolated places for the next four days till July 27.\n\nIn Chandigarh and Punjab, \"above normal\" temperatures with high humidity are predicted for the next two days. Light to moderate rainfall is forecasted in other parts of north and south Odisha over the next two days, with similar conditions expected on July 25 and 26. Heavy to very heavy rainfall is anticipated in the North Goa and South Goa districts from July 24 to 25.\n\nAir Quality Index\n\nThe Air Quality Index (AQI) of the national capital was recorded in the \"good\" category with a reading of 40, according to the Central Pollution Control Board.\n\nRecent Weather Changes\n\nOn Monday, Delhi witnessed a sudden weather change with heavy rain lashing parts of the city. The maximum temperature was recorded at 36.2 degrees Celsius, slightly above normal. The relative humidity at 5:30 pm stood at 68%. The rain contributed to the monthly total, but Delhi still faces a deficit, requiring one to two more spells of moderate rain to meet the average for July.\n\nHighest Rainfall in June\n\nIn June, Delhi recorded its highest rainfall in 88 years, with 228 mm of rainfall recorded between 8:30 am on June 27 and 8:30 am on June 28. A total of 235.5 mm of rain was recorded, marking the maximum rainfall in 24 hours in June since 1936.\n\nIMD Forecasts and Observations\n\nAccording to IMD officials, light to moderate rainfall was logged in various parts of Delhi on Monday. The Safdarjung observatory recorded 31.4mm of rainfall between 8:30 am and 5:30 pm. Despite this, Delhi remains in deficit for July. Mahesh Palawat, vice president at Skymet, noted that the monsoon trough's position south of Delhi and closer to central India is why significant rain has been sparse. He added, \"Every time the trough moves closer to Delhi -- as it did on Monday -- Delhi logs an increase in rain intensity.\"\n\nThe IMD data highlighted that after Monday's rain, Delhi's monthly total for July is now 118.2mm, short of the average 143.4mm normally recorded till July 21.
